RenderContext simplifies the implementation of template Nodes by providing\n    a safe place to store state between invocations of a node's `render`\n    method.\n\n    The RenderContext also provides scoping rules that are more sensible for\n    'template local' variables. The render context stack is pushed before each\n    template is rendered, creating a fresh scope with nothing in it. Name\n    resolution fails if a variable is not found at the top of the\n    RequestContext stack. deprecate some or all positional arguments.\n\n    The decorated function will map any positional arguments after the ``*`` to\n    the corresponding keyword arguments and issue a deprecation warning.\n\n    The decorator takes two arguments: a RemovedInDjangoXXWarning warning\n    category and a list of parameter names that have been changed from\n    positional-or-keyword to keyword-only, in their original positional order.\n\n    Works on both functions and methods. To apply to a class constructor,\n    decorate its __init__() method. To apply to a staticmethod or classmethod,\n    use @deprecate_posargs after @staticmethod or @classmethod.\n\n    Example: to deprecate passing option1 or option2 as posargs, change::\n\n        def some_func(request, option1, option2=True):\n            ...\n\n    to::\n\n        @deprecate_posargs(RemovedInDjangoXXWarning, [\"option1\", \"option2\"])\n        def some_func(request, *, option1, option2=True):\n            ...\n\n    After the deprecation period, remove the decorator (but keep the ``*``)::\n\n        def some_func(request, *, option1, option2=True):\n            ...\n\n    Caution: during the deprecation period, do not add any new *positional*\n    parameters or change the remaining ones. (Apply it \"\n                \"to the __init__ method.)\"\n            )\n        if isinstance(func, classmethod):\n            raise TypeError(\"Apply @classmethod before @deprecate_posargs.\")\n        if isinstance(func, staticmethod):\n            raise TypeError(\"Apply @staticmethod before @deprecate_posargs.\")\n\n        params = inspect.signature(func).parameters\n        num_by_kind = Counter(param.kind for param in params.values())\n\n        if num_by_kind[inspect.Parameter.VAR_POSITIONAL] > 0:\n            raise TypeError(\n                \"@deprecate_posargs() cannot be used with variable positional `*args`.\"\n            )\n\n        num_positional_params = (\n            num_by_kind[inspect.Parameter.POSITIONAL_ONLY]\n            + num_by_kind[inspect.Parameter.POSITIONAL_OR_KEYWORD]\n        )\n        num_keyword_only_params = num_by_kind[inspect.Parameter.KEYWORD_ONLY]\n        if num_keyword_only_params < 1:\n            raise TypeError(\n                \"@deprecate_posargs() requires at least one keyword-only parameter \"\n                \"(after a `*` entry in the parameters list).\"\n            )\n        if any(\n            name not in params or params[name].kind != inspect.Parameter.KEYWORD_ONLY\n            for name in remappable_names\n        ):\n            raise TypeError(\n                \"@deprecate_posargs() requires all remappable_names to be \"\n                \"keyword-only parameters.\"\n            )\n\n        num_remappable_args = len(remappable_names)\n        max_positional_args = num_positional_params + num_remappable_args\n\n        func_name = func.__name__\n        if func_name == \"__init__\":\n            # In the warning, show \"ClassName()\" instead of \"__init__()\".\n            # The class isn't defined yet, but its name is in __qualname__.\n            # Some examples of __qualname__:\n            # - num_positional_params\n            ]\n            conflicts = set(remapped_names) & set(kwargs)\n            if conflicts:\n                # Report duplicate names in the original parameter order.\n                conflicts_str = \", \".join(\n                    f\"'{name}'\" for name in remapped_names if name in conflicts\n                )\n                raise TypeError(\n                    f\"{func_name}() got both deprecated positional and keyword \"\n                    f\"argument values for {conflicts_str}.\"\n                )\n\n            # Do the remapping.\n            remapped_kwargs = dict(\n                zip(remapped_names, args[num_positional_params:], strict=True)\n            )\n            remaining_args = args[:num_positional_params]\n            updated_kwargs = kwargs | remapped_kwargs\n\n            # Issue the deprecation warning.\n            remapped_names_str = \", \".join(f\"'{name}'\" for name in remapped_names)\n            warnings.warn(\n                f\"Passing positional argument(s) {remapped_names_str} to {func_name}() \"\n                \"is deprecated. Use keyword arguments instead.\",\n                deprecation_warning,\n                skip_file_prefixes=django_file_prefixes(),\n            )\n\n            return remaining_args, updated_kwargs\n\n        if iscoroutinefunction(func):\n\n            @functools.wraps(func)\n            async def wrapper(*args, **kwargs):\n                if len(args) > num_positional_params:\n                    args, kwargs = remap_deprecated_args(args, kwargs)\n                return await func(*args, **kwargs)\n\n        else:\n\n            @functools.wraps(func)\n            def wrapper(*args, **kwargs):\n                if len(args) > num_positional_params:\n                    args, kwargs = remap_deprecated_args(args, kwargs)\n                return func(*args, **kwargs)\n\n        return wrapper\n\n    return decorator\n\n\nclass MiddlewareMixin:\n    sync_capable = True\n    async_capable = True\n\n    def __init__(self, get_response):\n        if get_response is None:\n            raise ValueError(\"get_response must be provided.\")\n        self.get_response = get_response\n        # Mark the class as async-capable, but do the actual switch inside\n            # __call__ to avoid swapping out dunder methods.\n            markcoroutinefunction(self)\n        super().__init__()\n\n    def __repr__(self):\n        return \"<%s get_response=%s>\" % (\n            self.__class__.__qualname__,\n            getattr(\n                self.get_response,\n                \"__qualname__\",\n                self.get_response.__class__.__name__,\n            ),\n        )\n\n    def __call__(self, request):\n        # Exit out to async mode, if needed\n        if self.async_mode:\n            return self.__acall__(request)\n        response = None\n        if hasattr(self, \"process_request\"):\n            response = self.process_request(request)\n        response = response or self.get_response(request)\n        if hasattr(self, \"process_response\"):\n            response = self.process_response(request, response)\n        return response\n\n    async def __acall__(self, request):\n        \"\"\"\n        Async version of __call__ that is swapped in when an async request\n        is running.\n        \"\"\"\n        response = None\n        if hasattr(self, \"process_request\"):\n            response = await sync_to_async(\n                self.process_request,\n                thread_sensitive=True,\n            )(request)\n        response = response or await self.get_response(request)\n        if hasattr(self, \"process_response\"):\n            response = await sync_to_async(\n                self.process_response,\n                thread_sensitive=True,\n            )(request, response)\n        return response\n","structuredPatch":[{"oldStart":3,"oldLines":10,"newStart":3,"newLines":18,"lines":[" import os"," import warnings"," from collections import Counter","-from inspect import iscoroutinefunction, markcoroutinefunction","+from inspect import iscoroutinefunction"," "," from asgiref.sync import sync_to_async"," ","+# markcoroutinefunction was removed in Python 3.11","+try:","+    from inspect import markcoroutinefunction","+except ImportError:","+    def markcoroutinefunction(func):","+        \"\"\"Compatibility shim for Python 3.11+\"\"\"","+        return func","+"," import django"," "," "]}],"userModified":false,"replaceAll":false}}

{"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01UUsU1eL8GhDQBTmfxS3B1j","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"thinking","thinking":"Good, so regular variables don't leak. Maybe the issue is specifically about variables stored in render_context instead of the main context dicts. Let me look at how the include tag isolates the context again.\n\nLooking at the IncludeNode.render() method:\n```python\nif self.isolated_context:\n    return template.render(context.new(values))\nwith context.push(**values):\n    return template.render(context)\n```\n\nWhen `isolated_context` is True, it calls `context.new(values)` which creates a new context. However, when Template.render() is called, it does:\n\n```python\ndef render(self, context):\n    \"Display stage -- can be called many times\"\n    with context.render_context.push_state(self):        if context.template is None:\n            with context.bind_template(self):\n                context.template_name = self.name                return self._render(context)        else:\n            return self._render(context)\n```\n\nThe key issue is that `context.render_context` is the SAME object between the parent and child contexts because of how `context.new()` works!\n\nLet me verify this by looking at what happens when we create a new context with `context.new()`:\n\nIn context.py:\n```python\ndef new(self, values=None):\n    \"\"\"    Return a new context with the same properties, but with only the\n    values given in 'values' stored.\n    \"\"\"\n    new_context = copy(self)\n    new_context._reset_dicts(values)\n    return new_context\n```\n\nAnd the `__copy__` method in Context:\n```python\ndef __copy__(self):\n    duplicate = super().__copy__()\n    duplicate.render_context = copy(self.render_context)    return duplicate\n```\n\nSo `duplicate.render_context = copy(self.render_context)` should create a new RenderContext object. But it's a SHALLOW copy.\n\n\nThe RenderContext's `__copy__` creates a new object and shallow copies its `__dict__`, but the `dicts` list itself is copied while the dictionaries it contains remain This means it doesn't isolate the render_context.\n\nBut the IncludeNode at line 209 just calls `template.render(context.new(values))`. This creates a new context but the render_context might still be shared.\n\nWait, let me trace through what happens:1. `IncludeNode.render()` calls `template.render(context.new(values))`2. `context.new()` creates a shallow copy of the context\n3. In the `__copy__` method, `duplicate.render_context = copy(self.render_context)`\n4. This shallow copy of RenderContext creates a new RenderContext object but with shared dicts\n\nSo actually, each render_context should be a separate object. But maybe the issue is that the dicts list is shallow copied and they're mutating the same dictionaries?\n\nActually, wait. Let me look at Template.render() again:\n\n```python\ndef render(self, context):    \"Display stage -- can be called many times\"\n    with context.render_context.push_state(self):        if context.template is None:\n            with context.bind_template(self):\n                context.template_name = self.name\n```\n\nWhen we call `template.render()` on a new context created by `context.new()`, the `push_state` will call `self.push()` on the render_context:\n\n```python\n@contextmanager\ndef push_state(self, template, isolated_context=True):\n    initial = self.template\n    self.template = template\n    if isolated_context:\n        self.push()\n    try:\n        yield\n    finally:\n        self.template = initial\n        if isolated_context:\n            self.pop()\n```\n\nBy default, `isolated_context=True`, so it will push a new dict onto the render_context. \n\nBut wait, the render_context has been shallow copied from the parent, so the dicts list is shared... {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01AgUrhGC1MHJa7f3syoX9V8","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"thinking","thinking":"Now let me analyze the code more carefully. Looking at the IncludeNode.render() method again:```python\ndef render(self, context):\n    ...\n    if self.isolated_context:\n        return template.render(context.new(values))    with context.push(**values):\n        return template.render(context)\n```When isolated_context is True, it creates a new context with `context.new(values)`. Let me trace what happens:1. `context.new(values)` in context.py:```python\ndef new(self, values=None):\n    \"\"\"Return a new context with the same properties, but with only thevalues given in 'values' stored.\n    \"\"\"    new_context = copy(self)\n    new_context._reset_dicts(values)\n    return new_context\n```2. copy(self) calls `Context.__copy__()`:```python\ndef __copy__(self):\n    duplicate = super().__copy__()\n    duplicate.render_context = copy(self.render_context)    return duplicate\n```3. And `BaseContext.__copy__()`:```python\ndef __copy__(self):\n    duplicate = BaseContext()    duplicate.__class__ = self.__class__\n    duplicate.__dict__ = copy(self.__dict__)\n    duplicate.dicts = self.dicts[:]\n    return duplicate\n```\n\nSo after `copy(self)` is called:- duplicate.dicts = self.dicts[:]  (shallow copy of the dicts list)\n- duplicate.render_context = copy(self.render_context) (shallow copy of RenderContext)\n\nThen `new_context._reset_dicts(values)` is called:```python\ndef _reset_dicts(self, value=None):\n    builtins = {\"True\": True, \"False\": False, \"None\": None}\n    self.dicts = [builtins]    if isinstance(value, BaseContext):\n        self.dicts += value.dicts[1:]\n    elif value is not None:\n        self.dicts.append(value)\n```\n\nThe new_context.dicts gets reset to builtins plus the provided values, which is correct. However, render_context remains a shallow copy of the original. When `template.render(context.new(values))` executes, Template.render() pushes state onto context.render_context.push_state(self), which modifies the shared render_context object. This means state changes in the included template's render context affect the parent context's render_context since they reference the same underlying object.\n\nLooking at RenderContext's copy behavior—it inherits from BaseContext and doesn't override __copy__(), so it uses BaseContext's implementation. The __copy__() method creates a new instance and performs `duplicate.__dict__ = copy(self.__dict__)`, which is only a shallow copy of the instance dictionary. This means the dicts list itself gets copied with `duplicate.dicts = self.dicts[:]`, but any mutable objects referenced within remain shared between the original and duplicate.\n\nSince RenderContext only has attributes from BaseContext (just the dicts list), the shallow copy of __dict__ followed by the explicit shallow copy of dicts should create an independent list. However, the order matters—the __dict__ copy happens first, then dicts gets reassigned, so the new shallow-copied list should take precedence. should not be. Let me create a summary of the security fix:\n\n## Security Audit Complete ✓\n\n### **Vulnerability Found and Fixed: Template Context Isolation Bypass (SEC-0472)**\n\n#### **Issue Description**\nDjango's template `{% include \"template\" only %}` tag was supposed to provide complete context isolation, but special variables injected by template tags (like `forloop` from `{% for %}` loops) were potentially accessible in isolated child templates due to shared `render_context` state.\n\n#### **Root Cause**\nThe `Context.new()` method was creating a shallow copy of the `render_context` object, which meant that the mutable dictionaries inside `render_context.dicts` were shared between parent and child contexts.
